  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_38fc47d9-0212-4091-bfd3-03542c27c39b'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText17189125781722593831" style="display:none">John Difool, a low-class detective in a degenerate dystopian world, finds his life turned upside down when he discovers an ancient, mystical artifact called "The Incal." Difool's adventures will bring him into conflict with the galaxy's greatest warrior, the Metabaron, and will pit him against the awesome powers of the Technopope. These encounters and many more make up a tale of comic and cosmic proportions that has Difool fighting for not only his very survival, but also the survival of the entire universe.</span>

<div id="review_2566843675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2566843675" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2566843675?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2018-comics">2018-comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2566843675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2821699133115246376">Down and out class R detective John DiFool has a powerful artifact, The Incal, fall into his grasp. But what is the Incal? And what will other people do to get it?<br/><br/>Yeah, that's grossly oversimplifying it but The Incal throws so many concepts at you it's hard to simplify. Do I mention the far-future, near dystopian setting where most of humanity spends most of its time watching TV? Or the giant flying space jellyfish? Or the dark eggs? Or The Metabaron, the biggest bad ass in the galaxy? Or the Pr</span>
  <span id="freeText2821699133115246376" style="display:none">Down and out class R detective John DiFool has a powerful artifact, The Incal, fall into his grasp. But what is the Incal? And what will other people do to get it?<br /><br />Yeah, that's grossly oversimplifying it but The Incal throws so many concepts at you it's hard to simplify. Do I mention the far-future, near dystopian setting where most of humanity spends most of its time watching TV? Or the giant flying space jellyfish? Or the dark eggs? Or The Metabaron, the biggest bad ass in the galaxy? Or the Prezident and his hunchbacks? Or the conjoined twins that rule the empire, The Emperoress?<br /><br />The story starts at street level with John DiFool finding the Incal and scales up a few times until it's the ultimate battle between light and darkness with the entire universe at stake. Jodorowsky throws idea after idea at the reader without much breathing room.The story gets a little incoherent at times but it's best to hold on and pay attention as best you can. I have to think Grant Morrison borrows a lot from this. <br /><br />The art is by Moebius and is quintessential Moebius: an orgy of clean lines and minimalist but still intricate art. I'm a little saddened that it's taken me this long to discover Moebius but I'm glad I have a lot his comics ahead of me. The presentation, with the original colors on slick paper, is akin to the Dark Horse Moebius Library. It's built to last and I plan on putting it to the test.<br /><br />Things got really crazy toward the end. I'd say The Incal is more about the journey and the ideas along the way than the destination. While I enjoyed this quite a bit, I think I'll leave John DiFool's other adventures on the shelf. The poor bastard has been through enough!<br /><br />While I didn't like this one quite as much as World of Edena, I'll be tracking down more of Humanoids' Moebius titles some time soon. 4.5 out of 5 stars.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2821699133115246376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7858793-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546468430p2/7858793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/996597145?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/7858793-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7858793-alex?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7858793-alex?shelf=comics-graphic-novels">comics-graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer996597145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10922844669345340443">I think that seeing the documentary <i>Jodorowski's Dune</i> helped prepare me for this book, since I knew what I was getting into. In a lot of ways, <i>The Incal</i> does what Jodorowski wasn't able to do with his film adaptation of Frank Herbert's novel. <br/><br/>As far as I can tell, <i>The Incal</i> is about...proto-scientific neo-spiritual existentialism? That sounds about right. In a weird way, this story reminded me of C.S. Lewis's <i>Space Trilogy</i>--not a connection I was expecting to make as I read this. <br/><br/>My suggestion f</span>
  <span id="freeText10922844669345340443" style="display:none">I think that seeing the documentary <i>Jodorowski's Dune</i> helped prepare me for this book, since I knew what I was getting into. In a lot of ways, <i>The Incal</i> does what Jodorowski wasn't able to do with his film adaptation of Frank Herbert's novel. <br /><br />As far as I can tell, <i>The Incal</i> is about...proto-scientific neo-spiritual existentialism? That sounds about right. In a weird way, this story reminded me of C.S. Lewis's <i>Space Trilogy</i>--not a connection I was expecting to make as I read this. <br /><br />My suggestion for tackling <i>The Incal</i> is to leave your expectations of traditional storytelling at the door. It starts weird, and gets weirder, so it's more important to just appreciate the unbridled creativity that Jodorowski and Moebius bring to life. If you spend time trying to find the threads of an actual narrative here, it'll just drive you nuts every time someone yells, "Oh no! The Necrodroid!" or "Quickly, Metabaron! We must stop the shadow egg from devouring the sun!" Just don't ask questions and you'll be fine.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10922844669345340443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_445573038" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/445573038" />
    <a title="Sean Francisco Yau-Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1175602-sean-francisco-yau-smith"><img alt="Sean Francisco Yau-Smith" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/445573038?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Francisco Yau-Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Francisco Yau-Smith" href="/user/show/1175602-sean-francisco-yau-smith">Sean Francisco Yau-Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1175602-sean-francisco-yau-smith?shelf=graphic-novels-my-criterion-collec">graphic-novels-my-criterion-collec</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer445573038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10846057618607099444"><br/>When Jean Giraud or Moebius passed away, the international "comic book" or "graphic novel" lost the last of the 4 great giants who shaped the medium (the other three being Osamu Tezuka, Will Eisner and Jack Kirby)- geniuses who combined an innovative and unique look and feel, with a tremendous breadth of work. While American exposure to Moebius actual comic book work was limited- his overall effect in terms of design and mass media can't be understated - first through the translations of "Metal </span>
  <span id="freeText10846057618607099444" style="display:none"><br />When Jean Giraud or Moebius passed away, the international "comic book" or "graphic novel" lost the last of the 4 great giants who shaped the medium (the other three being Osamu Tezuka, Will Eisner and Jack Kirby)- geniuses who combined an innovative and unique look and feel, with a tremendous breadth of work. While American exposure to Moebius actual comic book work was limited- his overall effect in terms of design and mass media can't be understated - first through the translations of "Metal Hurlant" into "Heavy Metal"- but then coming to full fruition as designer for "Alien", "Tron", Blade Runner" and "The Fifth Element". Arguably, while the techno-fetish side of cyber-punk was influenced by Japanese Manga (Otomo's "Akira")- Giraud gave it the "film-noir" aspect. And of course- cyber-punk went and informed everything else.<br /><br />To re-read The Incal- is to revisit and artist at his creative prime, working with his best life-long collaborator - Alejandro Jodorowsky. The result is a great visual jazz riff between the two. Moebius lays down sheet after of stunning visual layouts and details- while Jodorowsky's plot twists and turns keep you running with the momentum. Reading this now, 30 years after it's launch, a lot might seem familiar- the work influenced a lot of current science fiction - "the Fifth Element" and even the Matrix- but that's because this is the source material for what we see now.<br /><br />TBH- a feel this piece time-travels a lot better than "The Watchmen" or "Dark Knight"- it maintains a fresh, vital take on the world around it. <br /><br />Hopefully, more of Moebius work will finally make it to the US. In the meantime don't miss this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10846057618607099444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1060790780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1060790780" />
    <a title="Blake Ellis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8663495-blake-ellis"><img alt="Blake Ellis" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1060790780?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blake Ellis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blake Ellis" href="/user/show/8663495-blake-ellis">Blake Ellis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1060790780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8161977665982520605">Moebius: Great at art. Genius of western comics. <br/><br/>Jodorowsky: Great concepts, but has the biggest, dumbest lead foot when it comes to execution. At the very least, can someone call a cease-fire to his out of control use of exclamation points? If you expect character development, coherent plot, robust and convincing dialogue, and any respect for subtlety at all, apply elsewhere. In fairness to Jodo - his films are amazing when any pretense of these elements of storytelling are bypassed completely.</span>
  <span id="freeText8161977665982520605" style="display:none">Moebius: Great at art. Genius of western comics. <br /><br />Jodorowsky: Great concepts, but has the biggest, dumbest lead foot when it comes to execution. At the very least, can someone call a cease-fire to his out of control use of exclamation points? If you expect character development, coherent plot, robust and convincing dialogue, and any respect for subtlety at all, apply elsewhere. In fairness to Jodo - his films are amazing when any pretense of these elements of storytelling are bypassed completely. Surreal audiovisual experiences. But when you have something that resembles a plot, and you have enticing character concepts, and you have constant dialogue, and you have to spend more than two hours with it, it clearly kind of falls apart here. <br /><br /> I have to admit, I'd probably be more forgiving if everything Jodorowsky releases here in the states wasn't prefaced by some hyperbolic statements to the tune of "the books the form was made for." I wonder if these people read that much? Science fiction, comics, or otherwise?</span>
  <a data-text-id="8161977665982520605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_946117117" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/946117117" />
    <a title="Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31382574-andrew"><img alt="Andrew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535162065p2/31382574.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/946117117?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/31382574-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31382574-andrew?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31382574-andrew?shelf=i-own-wishlist">i-own-wishlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31382574-andrew?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer946117117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1138478243812473198">This book drips in pure sci-fi creativity. It seems like every page has a new, cool concept put forth; all within a cohesive narrative. (I won't give any examples, as I think that would take away from the enjoyment of reading this book).<br/><br/>Moebius's art is fantastic. The new reprinted of The Incal respectfully retains the original coloring (which is especially nice since many reprints seem to replace the original color with some awful modern rendering). I see so many artists that I love within Moeb</span>
  <span id="freeText1138478243812473198" style="display:none">This book drips in pure sci-fi creativity. It seems like every page has a new, cool concept put forth; all within a cohesive narrative. (I won't give any examples, as I think that would take away from the enjoyment of reading this book).<br /><br />Moebius's art is fantastic. The new reprinted of The Incal respectfully retains the original coloring (which is especially nice since many reprints seem to replace the original color with some awful modern rendering). I see so many artists that I love within Moebius. I imagine those artists reading the same pages that I was and falling in love with the style and later adopting it into their own.<br /><br />The story-telling is a bit dated, and I usually hate saying that something is worth a read for its supposed historical importance (as if I would have any conception of which books are historically important); but I can't help but see so many elements here that were used by latter creators like P. Craig Russell, Paul Pope, Frank Miller, and numerous sci-fi films, and would recommend a read on that basis alone. <br /><br />Brian Michael Bendis wrote a forward to the new edition which consists mostly of him getting angry at people ripping off The Incal. He claims, rightfully, that people should be inspired by the creative impulse that possessed Jodorowsky and Moebius to create this book. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1138478243812473198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3457659065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12186180665685806756">So, I finally get to read those classics of French sci-fi thanks to an Humble Bundle from Humanoids. <br/><br/>« But, aren’t you french ? »<br/><br/>Well, yes. But I’m not the kind of French to pay 15€ for 48 pages of comic, and to wait a year between two installments. <br/><br/>So, The Incal is the start of the whole Metabarons universe. We follow the misadventures of a low rather private eye caught into events bigger than himself. Is it good ? Yes, it’s written by Jodorowski. Is it well drawn ? Yes, it’s drawn by Moebius. </span>
  <span id="freeText12186180665685806756" style="display:none">So, I finally get to read those classics of French sci-fi thanks to an Humble Bundle from Humanoids. <br /><br />« But, aren’t you french ? »<br /><br />Well, yes. But I’m not the kind of French to pay 15€ for 48 pages of comic, and to wait a year between two installments. <br /><br />So, The Incal is the start of the whole Metabarons universe. We follow the misadventures of a low rather private eye caught into events bigger than himself. Is it good ? Yes, it’s written by Jodorowski. Is it well drawn ? Yes, it’s drawn by Moebius. <br /><br />However, I’ve heard for decades about the genius of Jodorowski and Moebius creation and, reading it now, I can’t help but notice it borrowed heavily from the pages of early Judge Dredd in its world building. Maybe it’s a coincidence. I don’t want to be sacrilegious. But, we have human bodies recycling à la Rezyk, snarky TV holofeeds, bloc wars, etc... That’s a lot of coincidences. <br /><br />Still, well worth the very low price of admission. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_319917299" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/319917299" />
    <a title="Simon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9096819-simon"><img alt="Simon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597842388p2/9096819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/319917299?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simon" href="/user/show/9096819-simon">Simon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781906838393" href="/book/show/12371484-the-incal">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9096819-simon?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9096819-simon?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9096819-simon?shelf=mad-frenchmen">mad-frenchmen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9096819-simon?shelf=america-south">america-south</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9096819-simon?shelf=europe-west">europe-west</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9096819-simon?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9096819-simon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9096819-simon?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9096819-simon?shelf=this-is-your-brain-on-theosophy">this-is-your-brain-on-theosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9096819-simon?shelf=1980s">1980s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319917299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13045885340750891089">One of the most impressive achievements in comic book art and science-fiction/fantasy storytelling, despite its ambition and complexity one of the best places to start with both Moebius' comic books and Jodorowsky's oeuvre. <br/><br/>This starts out as a futuristic hardboiled noir detective story with a couple matching supernatural artifacts as MacGuffins. However, the story ends up drawing in more weird alien races, galaxy-spanning feudal theocratic powers scheming for control over the known universe a l</span>
  <span id="freeText13045885340750891089" style="display:none">One of the most impressive achievements in comic book art and science-fiction/fantasy storytelling, despite its ambition and complexity one of the best places to start with both Moebius' comic books and Jodorowsky's oeuvre. <br /><br />This starts out as a futuristic hardboiled noir detective story with a couple matching supernatural artifacts as MacGuffins. However, the story ends up drawing in more weird alien races, galaxy-spanning feudal theocratic powers scheming for control over the known universe a la Frank Herbert's "Dune" and increasingly strange characters "the Incal" ends up turning into one of the weirdest head trips committed to printed page. Jodorowsky uses as a springboard to explore his complicated views about politics, religion, gender issues, mass media and a ton of other things through science-fiction allegory. Come to think of it, "The Incal"'s fusion of the hardboiled detective fiction and space opera genres is probably the best pulp fiction medium for that purpose: The former genre has a long tradition for tons of convoluted conspiracies and gambits piling up on each other as the plot unfolds, with the latter you can draw as much weird crap into the setting to use as metaphors as your philosophy demands. Another thing that holds all the peyote-munching religious mysticism and philosophizing together with the increasingly complicated space opera/film noir plot is the anti-hero John Difool, who is both a pitch perfect parody of the typical hardboiled detective and a convincing everyman figure who basically reacts to all the weird shit going on around him the same way most readers would in the same situation. It makes the strange universe and plot more believable, and adds a sense of humour.<br /><br />The artwork is also absolutely gorgeous even by Moebius' standards, and sets the gold standard to this day for both surprisingly colourful future noir high tech metropolises and neo-feudal space opera with machine-worshipping priesthoods, Habsburg/Ottoman-style feudal empires ruling entire galaxies and whatnot. You can tell that as different works as "Warhammer 40,000" and "The Fifth Element" borrowed a ton of ideas from this! Be sure to get the original 1980s prints with the bright and psychedelic colours, by the way, newer omnibus reprints use more realistic gritty colours that just don't feel right because the use of colour contrasts chosen for aesthetic effect over realism is a huge part of Moebius' appeal for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13045885340750891089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_345951059" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/345951059" />
    <a title="S.A. Hunter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4305391-s-a-hunter"><img alt="S.A. Hunter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442501792p2/4305391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/345951059?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S.A. Hunter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="S.A. Hunter" href="/user/show/4305391-s-a-hunter">S.A. Hunter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer345951059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1594315501702113322">I kept picking up this graphic novel, reading a few pages, only to then put it down again. I could never get into it. The story zooms everywhere and is very epic, but the characters are not really developed and the dialogue is at times kind of preachy. I don't know if it all reads better in the original French or not. This story is heavy in metaphysics, and it felt like a lot of the supposed profundity of the text whizzed over my head, or maybe Jodorowsky tried to jam too much into this one stor</span>
  <span id="freeText1594315501702113322" style="display:none">I kept picking up this graphic novel, reading a few pages, only to then put it down again. I could never get into it. The story zooms everywhere and is very epic, but the characters are not really developed and the dialogue is at times kind of preachy. I don't know if it all reads better in the original French or not. This story is heavy in metaphysics, and it felt like a lot of the supposed profundity of the text whizzed over my head, or maybe Jodorowsky tried to jam too much into this one story. Like I don't understand why he felt the need to introduce the five humors of John Difool, portrayed as funny little cartoon imps, when they didn't seem to add anything to the story or maybe that whizzed over my head, too. But there is a lot going on in this book and stuff is introduced on the fly that seems to be really big, but we don't get to spend any time on it. I thought maybe I wasn't really reading the first in a series and some of the characters were developed in previous stories, but though Jodorowsky wrote some prequels, this was supposed to be a standalone story. There are so many characters that we don't get to know any of them, except possibly Difool, and he just barely. Though I felt like I wasn't getting much of the story, I persevered because I'd never read a work drawn by Moebius and wanted to keep looking at his artwork, and I had to read to understand what the artwork was portraying. <br /><br />The introduction to this book was by Brian Michael Bendis, which consists of him beseeching the reader not to rip off this book. I admit many of the elements in this story were familiar from other stories, notably <i>The Fifth Element</i>. Jodorowsky and Moebius sued the director Luc Besson for copyright infringement. They didn't win their case, but I think they had plenty of cause, and I think Jodorowsky and Moebius' estate may want to take a hard look at the past series of <i>Dr. Who</i> because there are a lot of things that are very similar. I recognized the microscopic spaceship and possibly the protoqueen/the flesh as being from this book. I'm sure there are more. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1594315501702113322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3178952147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5291567472539127564">Simple amazing. The art, the concept, the execution. It's a multilevel sci-fi that speaks volumes on spirituality, religion, technology, sexuality, human sacrifice, the duality of man and the connection between these concepts and many more. "The Incal" is one of the best choices you'll ever make, yet another proof (of too many to count) of Moebius mastery and genius. He's truly transcendent, Jodo was lucky to share some of his light with this comic. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1888213427" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1888213427" />
    <a title="John Pistelli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/833943-john-pistelli"><img alt="John Pistelli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354053455p2/833943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1888213427?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Pistelli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Pistelli" href="/user/show/833943-john-pistelli">John Pistelli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781594650932" href="/book/show/26190565-the-incal">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/833943-john-pistelli?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/833943-john-pistelli?shelf=twentieth-century">twentieth-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1888213427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4968941269961061475">This classic 1980s science fiction graphic novel is the tale of John DiFool (i.e., the fool of the Tarot, representing humanity's freedom and stupidity) and his journey to save the cosmos in the company of his sometime lover Animah (i.e., his Jungian anima, or female aspect) and some other probably allegorical figures on behalf and with the aid of the titular Incal, a device incarnating the animating spirit of the universe. Rising from the ruins of Jodorowsky's abortive <i>Dune</i> adaptation, <i>The Inca</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4968941269961061475" style="display:none">This classic 1980s science fiction graphic novel is the tale of John DiFool (i.e., the fool of the Tarot, representing humanity's freedom and stupidity) and his journey to save the cosmos in the company of his sometime lover Animah (i.e., his Jungian anima, or female aspect) and some other probably allegorical figures on behalf and with the aid of the titular Incal, a device incarnating the animating spirit of the universe. Rising from the ruins of Jodorowsky's abortive <i>Dune</i> adaptation, <i>The Incal</i> is both ludicrous and sublime as a half-satirical and all-visionary tour of variously cosmic locales, from dystopian <i>noir</i> pit-cities to sea planets patrolled by giant jellyfish. <br /><br />Moebius's art weaves intricate grounds with cartoonish figures into a dense texture that accomplishes for the novel what the sometimes thin writing cannot—the creation of a world, or, in this case, a universe. Moebius is a giant, and I would not disparage him casually, but I would say that he is perhaps—in contrast to someone like Eisner or Tezuka—a great comics artist without necessarily being a great comics storyteller; his layouts here are often more muddled than delirious, and he even once resorts to arrows to lead the reader's eye across the confusingly arrayed panels. <br /><br />The writing often has a similarly counterproductive effect. I actually appreciate Jodorowsky's casually imaginative "never explain, never apologize" approach to his settings, which I prefer to elaborate expository "world building," but the characters are just as sketchy, some of them not even rising to the level of caricature or symbol. Given the length and complexity of the saga, the indifference bred by his approach to the characters sometimes makes it difficult to want to pick the book up again for any other reason than Moebius's delineation of the settings. Jodorowsky, like some other writers who want to communicate occult or magical beliefs (I would also point to <a href="https://johnpistelli.wordpress.com/2016/10/04/grant-morrison-and-chris-burnham-nameless/" rel="nofollow noopener">Grant Morrison</a>), too often substitutes archetypes for characters. But it easier to have a visionary experience with a work of fiction, in whatever medium, if we can inhabit the narrative by having a convincingly intersubjective relation to the fictional figures. We should come to care about the metaphysics <i>because</i> we care about the characters or narrative, not the other way around—as Dante understood. (My citation of Dante aside, Jodorowsky would no doubt regard my criticism as weak, bourgeois, American sentimentalism: "I shit on the United States of America!" he declares in <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jNas99oEXBU" rel="nofollow noopener">the BBC Moebius documentary</a>, referring in particular to American comics's need for heroes and their pathos.) <br /><br />Finally, I am puzzled by Jodorowsky's metaphysics as such. Over and over again, the novel invokes the union of opposites—dark and light, masculine and feminine—yet at the conclusion we meet a great-bearded father God. (Perhaps no surprise, given this book's treatment of sex and gender.) The possibility of progress and evolution is held out, but eventually we discern a bitter cycle in which The Fool cannot move forward. Finally, what are these characters' journeys even worth intrinsically if they have been so aided and motivated by the <i>deus ex machina</i> of The Incal? <br /><br />The grandeur of this book makes all my carping and caviling look petty, though. <i>The Incal</i> has been enormously influential on the science fiction and fantasy of our time. Even if I am right that it is lacking in certain particulars (characterization, philosophy), its landscapes and seascapes and spacescapes and psychescapes are so indelible, its mingled tone of scabrous misanthropy and visionary hope so distinctive (this is the basis, I assume, for Pascal Ory's comparison, in his afterword, of the book to <i>Don Quixote</i>), that <i>The Incal</i> will remain a classic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4968941269961061475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1531893129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1531893129" />
    <a title="C. Varn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1133754-c-varn"><img alt="C. Varn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510698891p2/1133754.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1531893129?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C. Varn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C. Varn" href="/user/show/1133754-c-varn">C. Varn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1531893129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14065611639074363299"> Jodorowsky's "The Incal" is a decidedly unique hard book to write about because it is an experience that is deeply engaging, profoundly uneven, narratively frustrating, and dripping with Jodorowsky's almost maniac and gonzo ideas. Jodorowsky's comics are as enigmatic as his films but often with less subtly in its symbolism. While certain characters do have some narrative consistency such as the Metabaron and John DiFool, most the characters seem to have total personality changes depending on th</span>
  <span id="freeText14065611639074363299" style="display:none"> Jodorowsky's "The Incal" is a decidedly unique hard book to write about because it is an experience that is deeply engaging, profoundly uneven, narratively frustrating, and dripping with Jodorowsky's almost maniac and gonzo ideas. Jodorowsky's comics are as enigmatic as his films but often with less subtly in its symbolism. While certain characters do have some narrative consistency such as the Metabaron and John DiFool, most the characters seem to have total personality changes depending on the plot. The parameters of the universe are also vague--alternately like a space opera and a Platonic dimensions of geometry. The dialogue is often terrible and borders on a blend of spiritual and techno-jargon. Still, in this comic, one can see the vision that launched a thousand ships. The epic strangeness is unique.<br /><br />If one is not already familiar with Jodorowsky, I strongly suggest starting with the 2014 documentary, Jodorowsky's Dune, and one can see clearly where the maniac genius of "The Incal" was born. The spiritual allegories are also rife in this work in ways that may be somewhat alien to people not familiar with Jodorowsky. Moebius's art as well as the original color work remains and really adds depth of character and interest to Jodorowsky's vision. <br /><br />I strongly suggest reading this even if I will freely admit that it is a far from perfect work. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14065611639074363299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3332897981" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3332897981" />
    <a title="Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/800291-andrew"><img alt="Andrew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295167791p2/800291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3332897981?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/800291-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781594650932" href="/book/show/26190565-the-incal">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3332897981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11128442786770560450">I will admit I am always a little cautious when reading a book which everyone seems to rave about - in the case of this book almost worship it would seem. The scope for disappointment and disillusionment is terrifying at the very least. <br/><br/>However somehow I seem to blunder in to reading them all the same, although in this case I will admit it was a conscious decision, a rather expensive one since this is the hardback version. <br/><br/>But what of the book, well I am still digesting it even though I finished</span>
  <span id="freeText11128442786770560450" style="display:none">I will admit I am always a little cautious when reading a book which everyone seems to rave about - in the case of this book almost worship it would seem. The scope for disappointment and disillusionment is terrifying at the very least. <br /><br />However somehow I seem to blunder in to reading them all the same, although in this case I will admit it was a conscious decision, a rather expensive one since this is the hardback version. <br /><br />But what of the book, well I am still digesting it even though I finished reading it yesterday. To say that it is immense and spectacular is an understatement. The imagination of the artwork is only matched by the scope of the storyline. True there are as grand if not more so stories out there however when everything is combined together you really do feel like you have been across the galaxy and back again. <br /><br />However even with all these high concepts and ideas the characters especially John DiFool are still easy to follow and sympathise with. To be honest I can see why other stories where written (although right now I have no idea how they work) as even after all that happened you still want to know more. <br /><br />And then there is the artwork - well you can see why so many people credit (and steal) ideas from it, it is truly sumptuous and rightfully so it is praised for it. I can easily see after reading only one book people become collectors of both Alejandro Jodorowsky and Moebius the genius behind the artwork.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11128442786770560450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinayak Hegde" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinayak Hegde" href="/user/show/57521234-vinayak-hegde">Vinayak Hegde</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57521234-vinayak-hegde?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57521234-vinayak-hegde?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3641033893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer770656885983663586">A low-class detective becomes the unexpecting hero of the eternal battle between light and darkness. There is a lot of metaphysical and religious allegory (you can see symbolism from Christianity, Buddhism, and Hinduism). However, the story arc felt a little flat with another twist around the corner without an overarching narrative and became tiresome after a while.<br/><br/>Jean Giraud's (Moebius) artwork is top-notch and ahead of its time. It's like watching Akira several decades back. The imagery and t</span>
  <span id="freeText770656885983663586" style="display:none">A low-class detective becomes the unexpecting hero of the eternal battle between light and darkness. There is a lot of metaphysical and religious allegory (you can see symbolism from Christianity, Buddhism, and Hinduism). However, the story arc felt a little flat with another twist around the corner without an overarching narrative and became tiresome after a while.<br /><br />Jean Giraud's (Moebius) artwork is top-notch and ahead of its time. It's like watching Akira several decades back. The imagery and the massive worlds depicted keep the story engaging with the intricate details and florid imagination. The coloring is also delightful. Much of the artwork is recycled from Jodorowsky's Dune adaptation that never got completed. <br /><br />5 stars for the artwork (which is exquisite) but only 3 stars for the middling story, averaging up to 4 stars overall.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_519359865" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/519359865" />
    <a title="Byron Georgalas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13702352-byron-georgalas"><img alt="Byron Georgalas" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/519359865?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Byron Georgalas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Byron Georgalas" href="/user/show/13702352-byron-georgalas">Byron Georgalas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781906838393" href="/book/show/12371484-the-incal">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer519359865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16848605966601270852">I am sorry, but I couldn't like "The Incal" as much as I wanted. Its art is what an epic space opera should be. Colossal scale but with attention to detail, really beautiful exotic environments with the necessary disregard of physics and it succeeded in immersing you in that degenerate galaxy. Being true to the sci-fi genre, it also dealt with pressing social subjects, like the indifference of the individual and the media manipulation by the leading elite, which allowed (in my view) the Darkness</span>
  <span id="freeText16848605966601270852" style="display:none">I am sorry, but I couldn't like "The Incal" as much as I wanted. Its art is what an epic space opera should be. Colossal scale but with attention to detail, really beautiful exotic environments with the necessary disregard of physics and it succeeded in immersing you in that degenerate galaxy. Being true to the sci-fi genre, it also dealt with pressing social subjects, like the indifference of the individual and the media manipulation by the leading elite, which allowed (in my view) the Darkness to creep.<br /><br />It was then, as I mentioned, a story of epic proportions, but the storytelling was lacking. The characters seemed to accept very easily every absurd idea that the Incal had, losing their individuality and, one could say, their own free will. The only one who revolted was John Difool, but in an incoherent, chaotic and seemingly unjustified way. Further, the pacing seemed rushed and there were many times where large jumps were made within the same page.<br /><br />For last, I left the dialogues who seemed for the most part quite uninspired and bland. Perhaps that was due to the translation from French, but unfortunately, unless I dedicate four years of my life to achieve mastery over that language, I will not learn first-hand if the quality in the dialogues was literally lost in translation.<br /><br />To sum it up, I enjoyed it, but it fell short. The three stars are for the general story, the universe and the artwork. Perhaps it was my high initial expectations. Perhaps I wasn't careful enough when I was reading it. Perhaps...I don't know. What I know is that I will certainly give it another chance.<br /><br />PS. In this particular edition, the typed text seemed too poor in oversized bubbles that were designed for the original (French) letters. Please, be more careful the next time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16848605966601270852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_653949347" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/653949347" />
    <a title="David Gallin-Parisi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1803950-david-gallin-parisi"><img alt="David Gallin-Parisi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1229321018p2/1803950.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/653949347?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Gallin-Parisi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Gallin-Parisi" href="/user/show/1803950-david-gallin-parisi">David Gallin-Parisi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1803950-david-gallin-parisi?shelf=videogames">videogames</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1803950-david-gallin-parisi?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer653949347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2226046735344117658">The legendary, always-mentioned-but-rarely-seen, influential, and illustrious Mobius and Jodorowsky work is a must read for anybody interested in the following things. Bear with me, this is a long list. Check this out if you find yourself in any of these listings: fantasy lover, sci-fi dreamer, trip-mode druggy adventure, video games, Star Wars, art comics like Ben Jones' or CF's contemporary works, comics like X-Men or X-Whatever, desert dystopias, blade runner dystopias, rainbow industrial par</span>
  <span id="freeText2226046735344117658" style="display:none">The legendary, always-mentioned-but-rarely-seen, influential, and illustrious Mobius and Jodorowsky work is a must read for anybody interested in the following things. Bear with me, this is a long list. Check this out if you find yourself in any of these listings: fantasy lover, sci-fi dreamer, trip-mode druggy adventure, video games, Star Wars, art comics like Ben Jones' or CF's contemporary works, comics like X-Men or X-Whatever, desert dystopias, blade runner dystopias, rainbow industrial parks, moldy aliens, outer space, inner space, detective noir-ish characters, loners, goddesses, spiritual awakenings, and more. If you like ANY of the above, you've probably already seen parts of this work. This work has been so massive to so many writers, artists, film makers, and designers that much of The Incal seems already appeared; re-done, re-realized, appropriated, and re-inserted into so many mediums. Let's just say that after reading this I gained much new found admiration for Jodorowsky and Mobius, and lost even more respect for George Lucas. All that said, The Incal is rad in the farthest reaches of the work. This work is entirely pleasurable and immersive. The original colors have been restored and feel like a luscious strip of candy dots, saturated with sugar and color, placed on your tongue for each page turned. Jodorowsky's writing keeps taking the story up and beyond to some next level shit, to paraphrase the dorks that will devour this. Video game lovers story progression. Plus all the gorgeous and intense tripped-out art. If you see this anywhere, buy on sight. Or check it out immediately from your library. Electric, heavy, streamlined, deep adventure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2226046735344117658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('H2d1ElRLeEYtygxTPOmWGxbLtpBedOdDdb5B+a2o8NiLhm4gA5TkEAlfnN57/LZ1Tln3jYejZ3HHsIDQ0XPySQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PK6qOhtxe9Zs9Y49OL2Aqytq/4h01PfjemeKwvkj6zeoT7EITK7ngEhgHrB/qKDFc/i+la0Dd9HIaUvrhfjppg==')})
  }

We\'re in the most extreme and utter region of the human mind. A dim, subconscious underworld. A radiant abyss where men meet themselves. Hell, Netley. We\'re in the most extreme and utter region of the human mind. A dim, subconscious underworld. A radiant abyss where men meet themselves. Hell, Netley. We\'re in Hell.&quot; \n\nHaving proved himself peerless in the arena of reinterpreting superheroes, Alan Moore turned his ever-incisive eye to the squalid, enigmatic world of Jack the Ripper and the Whitechapel murders of 1888. Weighing in at 576 pages, From Hell is certainly the most epic of Moore\'s works and remarkably and is possibly his finest effort yet in a career punctuated by such glorious highlights as Watchmen and V for Vendetta. Going beyond the myriad existing theories, which range from the sublime to the ridiculous, Moore presents an ingenious take on the slaughter. His Ripper\'s brutal activities are the epicentre of a conspiracy involving the very heart of the British Establishment, including the Freemasons and The Royal Family. A popular claim, which is transformed through Moore\'s exquisite and thoroughly gripping vision, of the Ripper crimes being the womb from which the 20th century, so enmeshed in the celebrity culture of violence, received its shocking, visceral birth. \n\nBolstered by meticulous research that encompasses a wide spectrum of Ripper studies and myths and coupled with his ability to evoke sympathies in such monstrous characters, Moore has created perhaps the finest examination of the Ripper legacy, observing far beyond society\'s obsessive need to expose Evil\'s visage. Ultimately, as Moore observes, Jack\'s identity and his actions are inconsequential to the manner in which society embraced the Fear: &quot;It\'s about us. It\'s about our minds and how they dance. Jack mirrors our hysterias. Faceless, he is the receptacle for each new social panic.&quot; \n\nEddie Campbell\'s stunning black and white artwork, replete with a scratchy, dirty sheen, is perfectly matched to the often-unshakeable intensity of Moore\'s writing. Between them, each murder is rendered in horrifying detail, providing the book\'s most unnerving scenes, made more so in uncomfortable, yet lyrical moments as when the villain embraces an eviscerated corpse, craving understanding; pleading that they &quot;are wed in legend, inextricable within eternity&quot;. \n\nThough technically a comic, the term hardly begins to describe From Hell\'s inimitable grandeur and finesse, as it takes the medium to fresh heights of ingenuity and craftsmanship. Moore and Campbell\'s autopsy on the emaciated corpse of the Ripper myth has divulged a deeply disturbing yet undeniably captivating masterpiece. —Danny Graydon<\/span>\n  <a <span id="freeTextContainer4007750934146917843"><i>Also credited as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15944264.Alexandro_Jodorowsky' title='Alexandro Jodorowsky' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alexandro Jodorowsky</a></i><br/><br/>Better known for his surreal films <i>El Topo</i> and <i>The Holy Mountain</i> filmed in the early 1970s, Alejandro Jodorowsky is also an accomplished writer of graphic novels and a psychotherapist. He developed Psychomagic, a combination of psychotherapy and shamanic magic. His fans have included John Lennon and Marilyn Manson.</span>
